Autumn

Little Western Paradise 180

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Not Understanding the Wanderer, He Peeks Through the Door and Pities the Young Girl; Wishing to Hear of Hardships, He Cherishes the Jade and Visits the Poor Family.

This Little Western Paradise Inn, being the largest inn in Xi'an City, naturally had important people coming and going, as well as insignificant people. Li Shilian and Jia Duocai, having eaten their fill, walked back feeling somewhat drunk and uncomfortable. They intended to return to their room and go to sleep. As they walked into their courtyard, they saw a glass-covered kerosene lamp hanging under the eaves, its glass shade swaying in the air, and the dim yellow light moving on the walls. In that light, they saw three people standing in the middle of the courtyard. One was the inn's tea server, whom they could see clearly. Another was a girl of about twenty, wearing a short jacket that barely covered her belly and a black skirt hiked up above her knees, revealing her snow-white thighs in leggings. Her hair was also cut short, flat at the back of her head. She was clearly a modern girl from beyond Tongguan. Although they couldn't see her face clearly in the kerosene lamp light, they could see the rouge on her cheeks, smeared in red patches, almost reaching her ears. She was standing very close to the tea server, chattering away. A modern girl standing in a dimly lit place and talking so intimately with an inn's tea server could not be a good thing. Li Shilian walked towards his room, glancing at the girl. The girl happened to turn her head and, seeing someone paying attention to her, seemed to smile faintly, but unfortunately, it was not clear in the darkness. (37)

Thirteen Abacuses All Became Nines 181

— Mei Xue

Peng Zu Needs to Reincarnate Five Hundred Times to Finish

Among the Freshmen in the university dormitories, there were people from Sichuan, Fujian, and mostly from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Guangdong.

A Shaoxing classmate said, "If we had a thirteen-digit abacus here, and we added to it one by one, how long would it take to add it until every digit became a nine?" A classmate replied without hesitation, "Probably ten years." The Shaoxing person shook his head, indicating that it was far off. Others guessed twenty or thirty years, forty or fifty years, or even a hundred years, but the Shaoxing person shook his head each time. Among them, a certain gentleman who was studious and thoughtful pondered for a while and said with a smile, "If a person could use an abacus from the moment they were born, and worked on the abacus for ten hours a day, except for sleeping, eating, and relieving themselves, until they died at the age of one hundred, they would still need to reincarnate four thousand times, and experience four hundred thousand years, to make every digit of the thirteen-digit abacus a nine." People said he was lying and asked him to demonstrate a practical method.

The gentleman calmly said, "If we can make two movements on the abacus's units digit every second, adding two ones, then we can add 120 in one minute, 7200 in one hour, 72000 in ten hours of work a day, 2,160,000 in one month, 25,920,000 in one year, and 2,592,000,000 in one hundred years. To get to 9,999,999,999,999, we would need to add 2,592,000,000,000 for four hundred thousand years. So, wouldn't a centenarian need four thousand lifetimes to finish? Even if we asked the eight-hundred-year-old Peng Zu to use the abacus, he would need to reincarnate five hundred times to complete the task of making every digit of the thirteen-digit abacus a nine."

Anecdotes 182

— (Bai Ying)

A certain lady proposed to break off her engagement to her fiancé. The fiancé said, "I haven't mistreated you! For you, I spent thousands of dollars, for you, I lost a good job, for you, I was kicked out of my family, for you..." The lady impatiently said, "I'm breaking up with you precisely because you lost your job, because you were kicked out of your family, and because you don't have any money to spend on me anymore!"

Daughter's Classic and Women's Issues 183

— Zi Wei

The *Daughter's Classic* is a book for women from the feudal era. It's all about how girls should conduct themselves, how to learn the Three Obediences and Four Virtues, how to be good wives and mothers, how to emulate the virtuous women of the past, and how a girl should live her life. From her daily life, diet, work, hygiene, to her thoughts and behaviors, it provides extremely detailed explanations, so that a girl who understands it transforms her thoughts and views on life into a single archetype, forever confined to a dark room, subject to the control and threat of old morals.

However, times have changed, and feudal old ideas have become the dregs of the era. A woman living in this modern society receives equal treatment and opportunities as a man. Women in the present era are considered liberated, able to socialize openly, be economically independent, and obtain employment based on their abilities and skills to solve their livelihood problems just like men.

However, every society has its own deformed development defects, so the issue of women's paths in life has both its extremely bright side and its extremely dark side. Naturally, modern women's issues are clearly more complex and difficult to deal with than before due to different social environments and ways of thinking.

I heard that the Star Film Company recently made a film called *Daughter's Classic*, which takes modern women's issues as its central theme and gives great inspiration. In it, it uses Double Tenth Day as a backdrop to delicately depict the joys and harmonies, as well as the tragic sorrows, that many women encounter in life, and points out a path to a correct answer. I think this should be the most suitable "bible" that modern women should definitely read!

Some Interesting Sounds 184

— (Yu)

When a locomotive starts, the large iron arms of the steam engine drive the wheels on the tracks, making a special sound. Hangzhou people imitate it, saying, "Eat it all, pawn it all! Eat it all, pawn it all!"

:::::::::::::::::::::::::

The firecrackers set off during the New Year make two sounds, one up and one down. Shaoxing people say, "The first sound is 'Poor!' The second sound is 'Gao!' (In the Shaoxing dialect, 'Gao' refers to death or completion)."

:::::::::::::::::::::::::

There are many blacksmith shops outside Fuzhou City, and they are still hammering iron late into the night. They often have three people each holding a long-handled hammer, swinging and striking in succession. Fuzhou people use their local dialect to imitate it, saying, "Enemy steals food, enemy steals food."

:::::::::::::::::::::::::

People in the Xiamen and Zhangzhou areas imitate the sound of cicadas like this: "Weave tightly, weave tightly! Weave tightly, weave tightly!" (Meaning to quickly weave to prepare for the cold, and the sound is very similar.)

:::::::::::::::::::::::::

Northerners imitate the sound of Jiangxi people mending bowls, saying "Zi Gu Zi" (meaning "taking care of oneself").

Building a New Fence Again 185

Royal Fragrance Drifting Record 186

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Fortunately, Qing Shan and the others had some foresight. Before the Empress Dowager set off, they had already informed the officials here, giving them plenty of time to carefully renovate this dilapidated county town, lest the Empress Dowager be displeased when she saw it. So, when the Empress Dowager ordered to inspect the city, everyone was not too flustered. After all, with eight or nine days of effort, no matter how incompetent these local officials were, they should have made some progress. At that time, their group, like the group at Tianjin Station, dressed in opulent clothing and respectfully prostrated themselves beside the station to welcome the Empress Dowager. However, their ranks were very low, and none of them caught the Empress Dowager's attention. As a result, they might as well have made the trip for nothing, only making the station more lively. Perhaps they didn't even see the Empress Dowager's face!

To everyone's surprise, after departing from the station, the highest-ranking local official led the way, slowly proceeding along several of the wider main roads. These streets were usually very dirty, but today they were all covered with a layer of yellow sand, completely hiding their original ugliness. Although I don't know what the Empress Dowager thought of this, I myself was really very unhappy with this temporary fix. Chinese people never want to put in the effort to do things properly early on, but always love to use clever methods at the last minute to gloss over the situation: this is a perfect example! Later, we passed a city gate, and Zhuan Hu Fa saw through this kind of illness. Because the engineering of the city gate was relatively more difficult, even with seven or eight days of preparation, it was impossible to renovate it, because it had been allowed to collapse without any repairs. It could only be left to stand there, crooked like a decrepit old man. (147)

Local Customs

Early Qing Dynasty Prices in Shanghai (Part 2) 187

— Shanghai Correspondent

Ten, Sugar: Top-grade white cane sugar was worth three to four fen of silver per catty in the late Ming Dynasty. During the Shunzhi reign, due to frequent maritime conflicts, the price rose to four qian of silver per catty. It was not until the Kangxi reign that sugar prices returned to their former levels. In the winter of the 20th year of Kangxi, white sugar was worth three fen of silver per catty, and brown sugar was only worth about one fen. By the 25th year of Kangxi, it became even cheaper, costing only 20 wen per catty, which was less than two fen of silver.

Eleven, Porcelain: Porcelain from Jiangxi was originally very precious. During the Chongzhen era, the finest quality items were worth three to five qian of silver each, while inferior items could be bought for about three to five fen of silver for ten pieces. In the early Shunzhi period, when Jiangnan was just pacified but military affairs had not ceased, porcelain could not be transported to Shanghai, so prices rose sharply. Even the worst quality bowls were worth four to five fen of silver each. At this time, wealthy families in Shanghai switched to using copper or tin utensils, while the poor had to use bamboo or wooden bowls. In the early Kangxi period, porcelain was once very cheap, with even the best quality items costing no more than one qian of silver. In the 13th year of Kangxi, due to Wu Sangui's rebellion, bandits rose up everywhere in Jiangyou (Jiangxi), and porcelain became very expensive again, just like in the early Shunzhi period. It was not until after the 27th year that prices returned to the low levels of the early Kangxi era.

Twelve, Ge Cloth (Kudzu Cloth): Ge cloth was mostly transported from Zhejiang, Guangdong, Jiangxi and other provinces. In the Ming Dynasty, it was originally for the use of gentry, scholars and officials, not ordinary people, so a bolt more than three zhang long was worth three taels of silver. By the Qing Dynasty, the quality of ge cloth gradually deteriorated, and the price also fell day by day. After the establishment of the Jianghai Customs in Shanghai in the 24th year of Kangxi and the opening of the sea ban, merchant ships gathered, and ge cloth became more and more abundant. The best quality was worth no more than one fen and five or six li of silver per chi, and the inferior quality was only worth seven or eight li per chi.

Thirteen, Cocoon Silk: Cocoon silk mostly came from Shandong, with the best quality being produced on pepper trees. In the late Ming Dynasty, the price was exceptionally expensive, worth about one tael of silver per chi. In the early Qing Dynasty, Jiahu (Jiaxing and Huzhou), Suzhou and Songjiang all imitated weaving, so the price became very cheap. The best quality was no more than one qian of silver per chi, and the second-best quality could be bought for three to four fen of silver per chi.

Fourteen, Eyeglasses: Since the Ming Dynasty, Western goods had arrived, with eyeglasses costing four to five taels of silver per pair. However, the goods were very scarce, and it was not easy for ordinary wealthy families to purchase them. After the Shunzhi period, Suzhou and Hangzhou were able to imitate them, so they were sold everywhere. The best quality only cost seven to eight fen of silver per pair, and the worst quality cost no more than two to three fen. However, Western nearsightedness eyeglasses still cost two taels of silver to buy a pair.

Fifteen, Seafood: In the early Qing Dynasty, the only type of seafood sold in Shanghai shops with a verifiable price was bird's nest. In the late Ming Dynasty, the price was eight qian of silver per catty. During the Shunzhi period, the price was about the same. After the Kangxi period, it became very expensive, costing four taels of silver per catty. From then on, it was rarely used except in the most extravagant banquets.

Sixteen, Stationery: Bamboo paper, seventy-five sheets per dao, was worth two fen of silver during the Chongzhen period. In the early Shunzhi period and the 13th year of Kangxi, due to the turmoil in Fujian, the price rose to one qian and four or five fen per dao. After the 26th year of Kangxi, it returned to the old price of two fen per dao, but the number of sheets was only seventy. Vermilion inksticks, each box weighing fourteen taels, cost eight to nine taels of silver in the early Shunzhi period, but only cost two qian and five fen in the early Kangxi period. The best-quality Qingtian frozen stone for seals cost only a little more than one tael of silver per liang. Inkstones made from Suzhou Guanyin Mountain stone could be worth two to three qian of silver each.

Seventeen, Medicinal Materials: Most medicinal materials were not produced locally. In the early Kangxi period, due to the unresolved military affairs in Sichuan and Guangdong, the market prices of several essential medicines soared unexpectedly. For example, aconite could sell for dozens of taels of silver per piece, turmeric cost more than two hundred taels per liang, and cinnamon also cost twelve to thirteen taels. By the Kangxi period, after peace was restored in all directions, aconite only cost one qian of silver per piece, turmeric only cost eight fen per liang, and cinnamon only cost five taels per catty.

Eighteen, Fragrant Spices: In the late Ming Dynasty, sandalwood cost four to five qian of silver per catty, and agarwood cost less than one qian per catty. In the early Shunzhi period, the prices were four times higher, and ordinary wealthy families hardly used them lightly. In the 18th year of Kangxi, it was rumored that sandalwood was used in the palace to wash utensils, so the market price plummeted to only two qian of silver per catty, and Daoists still mostly prohibited its use when setting up altars and building temples. Due to the great opening of the sea market, agarwood was transported in large quantities, and the price returned to its original state in the late Ming Dynasty.

The above is a general overview of Shanghai prices from the late Ming Dynasty to the early Qing Dynasty, forty to fifty years, recorded in the Shanghai County Annals, Dong Han's "San Gang Shi Lue," Ye Mengzhu's "Yue Shi Bian," Yao Tinglin's "Ji Shi," and other books, which are excellent historical materials for studying the social and economic conditions of Shanghai in the early Qing Dynasty.

Financial Silver Prices Soar Continuously, Standard Gold Plummets to 18 Yuan 6 Jiao 188

Reaching a New Low of 901 Yuan 1 Jiao

Central Bank Interventions Offer Some Support Mid-Market

Due to the continuous surge in overseas silver markets and persistent selling pressure, the gold market yesterday reached a new low of 901 yuan and 1 jiao. According to foreign wire reports, the British and American silver markets rose significantly. Although London spot gold remained flat, exchange rates narrowed, and U.S. prices rose, market sentiment remained extremely fearful. Reports of the assassinations of the French Foreign Minister and the King of Yugoslavia caused an immediate drop upon market opening. Off-market pre-market trading struggled around 10 yuan, creating considerable confusion. After opening, prices rebounded from the lows but failed to break through the 10-yuan mark. As a result, the foreign exchange market was loose and oversupplied. Despite the Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's (HSBC) upward adjustments to both British and American exchange rates, market sentiment remained weak, gradually trending downward. However, there were numerous struggles along the way. Due to the extremely uneasy sentiment among bulls, even substantial support proved ineffective. The foreign exchange market fueled selling pressure, hardening repeatedly. Supply in the market exceeded demand, and buyers were temporarily constrained, causing a sharp decline to a new low of 902 yuan and 2 jiao. Subsequently, the wave of liquidations gradually subsided, and bargain hunters began to become active. Banks also seized the opportunity to consolidate positions, gradually pushing up gold prices. By noon, a sudden rally emerged, and market sentiment slightly strengthened, with the underlying trend turning positive. The market displayed a demand-exceeding-supply situation, with buying interest seemingly reviving. The noon close was stable. In the afternoon market, the opening price was lower due to loosened domestic trading. Although there was an initial dip, market sentiment remained relatively positive, leading to a rebound after the low. However, upon news of a rise in Bombay gold prices, selling pressure returned, causing a pullback. Despite some consolidation, market sentiment lacked vigor, and the overall trend gradually weakened. Further news from Bombay, reporting a rise of one anna, a fall of one anna, and then no change, led to a slight rebound after the low, but market sentiment ultimately trended downward, with many participants liquidating positions. Before the close, another new low of 901 yuan and 1 jiao was reached. Overall market sentiment was weak. The Central Bank's intermittent interventions with spot gold offered some stimulus to buyers, resulting in some rebound strength. However, the overall trend was perceived as deteriorating, and most bulls were hesitant to try easily, ultimately making it difficult to sustain. The difference between the December new standard and the old standard reached 2.5 yuan. Rumors circulated in the market that certain major speculators were planning significant downward moves. Page 19

Free Talk

Life at Twenty 205

— Gu Xi

The Japanese author Natsume Soseki once said, "One knows the benefits of life at twenty," which roughly means that ordinary people, having lived in this world for twenty years, understand the value of living and the joy of living. I cannot agree with this statement!

Speaking for myself, I have just reached this age this year, but I have never experienced this "benefit of life"! On the contrary, the idea that "life is not easy" is what I have been deeply tasting recently!

All of life's burdens and worries are like heavy bags of sand and stones pressing on the thin backs of laborers. At this point, they begin to tighten on our shoulders, making us feel that there is only suffering in the world! This suffering is often hidden from those under twenty by the colorful dreams of childhood!

Twenty years of heat and cold easily erode a person's childhood innocence and simplicity! At this time, he will begin to know that life is not as beautiful or easy as he imagined in the past! Before the age of twenty, people probably all lived with a slight smile. To tear apart this smile and make you believe that "things in life rarely go as you wish" is what this time is all about, making it impossible for you to smile.

Everyone's reason, emotion, and will all want to test their own wings at this age. But this contains a kind of crisis! Reason at twenty easily makes you hit a wall; emotion at twenty easily makes you fall; will at twenty easily makes you feel unfree! From here, a kind of sadness will lightly envelop your heart!

Zhu Guozhen of the Ming Dynasty said in "Yongchuang Small Notes": "After twenty, one is strong and self-reliant, eager to advance, regarding officialdom as easy to obtain, and chasing fame like pursuing goats." For such warriors who want official positions and fame, I can only stretch my neck and envy and bless them! As for myself, my own little wisdom over the past twenty years has made me lack this kind of courage to be "strong and self-reliant, eager to advance"! Although it is said that an official position can be pursued, I always feel that this matter is very difficult! As for "fame," I have never been very eager for it. Gorky said, "The ox has a good reputation, but it still has to fill its belly with hay!" Especially for people like me, fame is just a kind of restraint!

"Relying on parents, happily well-fed and warm, without worry or management, forgetting what is forgotten and lost"—the childlike era like a fairy tale has passed at twenty. After twenty, I have never felt the so-called value or joy of living in the world!

"Embracing the future: sadness always outweighs hope!" This is what I think, having spent twenty years in the world.

Night on the River Bottom (Continued) 206

— Liu Ming

"Where's Uncle?"

Because I was too bored and lonely in the evening, I asked like this.

"Uncle doesn't live here. He comes back in the middle of the night . . . . Oh, it's burnt. Smell that?" He quickly used the iron tongs to pull apart the fire and took out a piece of corn emitting smoke, acting as if he understood things better than I did.

At this time, the cabin door suddenly opened with a creak, and the dim light from the oil lamp inside the house spilled out like water. The mistress angrily appeared at the door, pulling her second son, who was standing in front of the door, and scolding him:

"You can't leave for a moment, you little devil, you want me to die!"

But looking at her face, the anger seemed to be put on. After walking to the fire and settling her second son with her eldest son, she quickly glanced at me as if to check if I had noticed her peeking at the bundle. I quickly avoided her gaze and took a piece of dry firewood to add to the fire.

"Waa waa waa" Another child burst into tears inside the house; this was the one she had carried inside earlier. She didn't pay any attention to him, only carefully warmed a clay pot filled with something in the fire, while loudly instructing her two children:

"Be careful! If you knock it over, I'll rip off your ears, you little devils!"

It seemed she was also showing off to me, but I found it very funny that she always called her children "little devils."

Perhaps it was because she was making dinner and had been constantly bending over that the baby strapped to her back started to cry along with an untamed yell. At this moment, she took the ladle in her hand, dipped it into the water tank with a slightly broken rim, making a heavy footstep like a man, ran into the house, and carried out the crying third child as if she were carrying a chicken or duck. After giving him a slap, she nimbly wiped his snot with her rough hand that had just hit him, flicking it away. Then, she grabbed the half-eaten corn in her eldest son's hand, scolding:

"You glutton!"

She immediately stuffed the snatched corn into her youngest son's mouth, forcefully blocking his crying mouth. At the same time, she cursed fiercely:

"Cry again! Cry again!"

This third child really stopped crying, but the smallest one crying on her back cried even louder. She reached back and slapped him several times before taking him off her back, opening the hole in her torn clothes in front of her chest, and putting her nipple into the child's small mouth. Thus, everything returned to peace, but the sound of the river behind the house was sent clearly and greatly into the room.

The eldest child, who had been deprived of his corn, first pouted his upper lip and deliberately scattered the small branches burning on the fire with a piece of dry firewood as thick as a wine cup. Then, he suddenly knocked over the water pot that his mother had told him not to touch, and the lid, water, and string beans immediately spilled out, and water vapor and smoke rose heavily.

"Heavens, you little devil, you . . . ."

The mistress started to cry hysterically, and the nursing baby also cried loudly.

The eldest child, who had caused the trouble, was hit by his mother and hid in a dark corner, sobbing softly, not daring to cry out loud.

▲ ▲ ▲

When it was time to sleep, I was led to a small room behind the store (probably where the grooms used to sleep), which emitted a musty smell that had been uninhabited for a long time. Dust-covered spider webs, in the dim yellow light of the vegetable oil lamp, hung like many tassels from the roof and in the four corners. The bed was made of three or four pine planks laid across two long benches. Other than that, there was neither a straw mat nor a cotton quilt.

"How can I sleep like this, landlady?"

I said after looking at the room. The mistress, who had just stepped out of the door, turned around and hugged the baby in her arms, her face stern and cold:

"I really can't help it, just make do, guest!" (To be continued)

Divine Facial Restoration 207

— Special Correspondent

In the "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio," a judge once replaced the ugly face of a woman with a beautiful one. There is a similar story in the West about a girl named Cinderella. Because she was born with an ugly appearance, her sisters always left her at home to do menial chores and clean up after parties when they went to balls. She was unkempt and ignored by everyone. Later, she moved a fairy, who used magic to transform her into a beautiful woman and took her to a ball where she met a prince who fell in love with her at first sight. When we read these stories, we naturally regard them as tales of gods and monsters. Who would have thought that with the progress of 20th-century science, there would actually be facts that seem similar to these stories?

This type of surgery is called "Plastic Surgery" in the medical field, which can be translated as "sculpting surgery," or simply "facial restoration." This is a new achievement in medical science. According to Professor Matutai, a famous French abdominal surgeon, "In ten or fifteen years, facial restoration will become the most important branch of surgery." Some in the British medical community also predict that in less than ten years, this type of surgery will become as common as general surgery.

It is said that this theory is not newly created. Eastern surgeons were already proficient in this method two thousand years ago, and what is even more surprising is that the method is the same as it is now. In the 16th century, Italian surgeons recorded dozens of cases of "skin grafting" surgery, all with good results. In 1597, Tagliacozzi first wrote a textbook on this technique. As for recent success, it is due to the war. This is indeed one of the few useful products created by the war.

Everyone knows the cruelty of modern warfare. When the flames of war ignite, flesh and blood fly everywhere. But it is over when one dies. The worst thing is to preserve life but be left with crippled limbs, especially incomplete facial features and a loss of original appearance. When family and friends meet, they do not recognize each other. Life is completely devoid of interest. When the European war ended in 1918, there were no less than hundreds of thousands of such wounded soldiers left behind. These became the materials for plastic surgeons to wield their knives and perform their skills. In quiet hospitals, month after month, they reconstructed their faces, restored their human form, and allowed them to no longer be scorned.

The largest of these hospitals is the Sidcup Facial Injuries Hospital, operated by the famous surgeon Sir Harold Gillies. Over several years, a total of 19,000 people were treated. Today, most of the exquisite facial restoration techniques of surgeons have been learned from this hospital. The results are almost unbelievable. A Canadian officer had his jaw blown away by a shell, and half of his face was destroyed. After months of work by the doctors, a new jaw was created for him, and his face was repaired inch by inch, even including his eyebrows. There are dozens of others whose faces have been reshaped to restore their human form. As for filling in deep scars on the face, that is countless. A doctor at the British Pension Department said, "This surgery is truly the work of gods, wonderfully indescribable."

In times of peace, this surgery has been transferred to repairing the damage inflicted on workers' bodies by industrial warfare. It is possible to take good skin, bones, cartilage, or nerves from the body to repair the damaged parts of the person. Let's give an example to illustrate. A chemical worker had a large part of the skin on his face eroded by acid, and it penetrated deep into the flesh. After being treated by a plastic surgeon, his face was first anesthetized with medicine, and the bleeding was stopped. Then the necrotic skin was scraped off, and a liquid was applied to the face, which slowly dried and formed a soft facial mask, becoming a model of the injured area. The model extended to the uninjured skin on the chest. Then, a large piece of skin of appropriate thickness was carefully removed from his body. This was the material for creating a new face. It was laid on the burned flesh, and then stitched firmly to the edges of the good skin. The skin and flesh there will naturally grow well, just like newly transplanted trees, they will naturally come alive. The blood vessels will extend out and connect with the veins and arteries. Once the traces of the stitches are gone, he will work as usual.

The thin skin needed for surgery can be obtained from many parts of the body. The area where the skin is cut will grow new skin in less than a month. Even if it is cut a little deeper, it does not matter, as long as thin skin is taken from elsewhere and laid on it. In the past, surgeons could only transplant small pieces of skin, but after an American doctor invented a method, the area of the skin could be enlarged. He discovered that if the pressure on the transplanted skin is evenly distributed on all sides, it can grow well. The effect of the pressure is to block the external blood supply, allowing the newly connected skin to settle in its own blood and lymph, while its blood vessels will extend out like the fine roots of a plant and connect with the overall flow of circulation.

Plastic surgery is progressing year by year. At first, it was just cutting skin to repair injuries, but now it can take skin, bone, cartilage, and nerves to create new faces and new facial structures. One patient had nerves on his face that could not move, and his face would obviously be stiff for the rest of his life. Later, after the doctor took great pains, he tried to connect nerves, cut open his thigh, took out an unimportant nerve, and connected it to his face, just like connecting broken wires with copper wire. In less than thirty days, the patient's face was able to move flexibly. After resting for a few months, his expressions were no different from ordinary people. This is the result of painstaking and meticulous research. There was also a girl whose face was completely destroyed. The doctor patiently repaired it for her. First, a section of rib was taken and carved into a new set of teeth. Then, a piece of skin was cut from her thigh to create eyelids and nostrils. Then, flesh was taken from the chest to fill the mouth and make lips, and cartilage was borrowed from the skull. After twenty-five "skin grafts," each time the skin had to be placed evenly and with extreme precision. In the end, a new face was created. Now you can meet this happy girl at banquets. In the future, bone grafting will also have amazing results. It is now possible to create a new thumb using the tibia and the flesh under the calf. In the future, it may even be possible to create a new hand.

This new technique, like other sciences, can also produce unexpected strange things. A woman had a torn lip, and the doctor repaired it with skin drooping from her cheek. Unexpectedly, every time her lip moved, she felt a sensation on her cheek. Even stranger, a patient had his throat rotted away, and the doctor repaired it with skin from his neck. Unexpectedly, eighteen months later, he felt uncomfortable swallowing things. It turned out that the new skin had grown whiskers inside... This incident has been confirmed by a medical journal.

In the past, the skin on the face could be tightened to reduce the appearance of aging, which everyone regarded as miraculous. But compared to today's facial restoration surgery, that facelift surgery is nothing. In the future, with the advancement of facial restoration surgery, it is possible that extremely ugly people can be transformed into beautiful ones. At that time, anyone who dislikes being old or ugly will be able to find Judge Lu everywhere.

Village Head (II)(X)(IV) 208

— Wang Renshu

"Therefore! Therefore!" Old Mu Ren gulped down a large mouthful of wine and said in a loud voice, "At this time, those with money should contribute money, and those with strength should contribute strength. Think about it, we old folks don't need to be said; the seventy-two strong men in the village, which one doesn't have a large string of old and young hanging behind him, relying on him for food and clothing. One day, they're drafted away. Are we going to let a large string of old and young starve to death? If those with money are unwilling to contribute, then they can only be forced to rebel! Forced onto Liangshan Mountain! At that time, you can't blame us!"

"Alas! Alas!" Mr. Feng Wen, who had been silent for a long time, finally opened his mouth. "The village...alas! Alas!...who can still afford to contribute money? Each family knows its own affairs, only the one who eats the bitter herb knows the bitterness. Which family in the village isn't struggling to make ends meet? Taxes are high, supplies are plentiful, expenses are high, and there's a lot of work to be done. Previous leaders also had their own hardships. Take me, for example, there's no hair to be found on an egg, I'm completely broke. My wife has no food to eat, and yesterday I already sent her to the city to help others. This debt-collecting son has also been taken to the city by his sister to be raised. You think there are many benefits to being a leader, but as for me, alas, don't even mention it, I'll definitely be leaving Niutou Village sooner or later. Village head, village head, I've had a good reputation my whole life, but I haven't gotten to eat mutton, and my mouth is full of the smell of sheep! I can't do this kind of bird business! It's really not something a human can do!"

"Alright! Alright!" Mr. Da Sheng found an opportunity to push him. "A Wen is the village head, only A Wen's name is known above. If your daughter leaves, who will the superiors look for in Niutou Village? I was originally helping A Wen. Fine, A Wen, you go! It'll save me the trouble too."

"Then there really will be a rebellion!" A Xian stood up from the bed. "As the saying goes, a snake cannot move without a head, if there is no leader, what will become of us!"

As A Xian spoke, he edged past the table and stood by the door. A burst of shouting came from outside.

"What's wrong? What's wrong? Who's hitting someone!" A Xian couldn't help but shout out.

A De and Kai Yang both squeezed towards the door.

I'm not doing this bird village police job anymore! I want the village head to give me justice! I want the village head to give me justice!"

As he got closer and closer, they gradually saw the bloodstains on his head!

"What's wrong?" Mr. Da Sheng and Mr. Feng Wen both put down their chopsticks and stood up! Only old Mu Ren was still lying on his buttocks, drinking his wine.

"What's wrong? What's wrong?"

"What's wrong? Hmph!" Duo Sheng limped into the house, spread his legs and stood still, saying, "Shou Fu Da Pao hit someone, Shou Fu Da Pao actually hit me like that! Shou Fu Da Pao actually hit me like that."

Kai Yang's mother, who was cooking the fire, also turned out from the inner room.

"Amitabha! What happened?"

Talking Points

Over 660,000 Imported Games and Toys 209

— Qiong Sheng

This year's promotion of "National Goods" was originally intended for both women and children, meaning that "mothers and children" could easily join together in patriotic actions. The result of the rallying cries is that perfumes and powders worth many tens of thousands were imported, and precious decorations and lace also amounted to many tens of thousands. This naturally makes people sigh that as the national crisis intensifies, "modernity" flourishes even more, echoing the lament that when a nation is about to perish, there will inevitably be monstrous things. However, the accompanying "children's national goods" have not won back many hearts either. According to reports, by mid-August of this year, imports of games and toys have reached a huge sum of over 660,000 national currency. Children, under the "earnest instructions" of adults, are not as addicted to luxury and dissipation as "modern" women, but they still cannot fulfill much of their patriotic responsibility. It really makes us wonder whether to grab these "ignorant children" and spank them, or blame whom?

Although these trivial ornaments are related to the great cause of the country and the nation, we have never blamed all the evils on women, and naturally we have no reason to blame it on children now. All consumption of luxury goods has become a symptom of the current social pathology. That is to say, the more bankrupt China's economy becomes, the more the desire for pleasure among a portion of the people increases, and the result must be the influx of "imported goods" to cater to this demand. It is not all Chinese women who use Parisian perfumes and powders, and it is not all children who can play with "foreign dolls" and all kinds of new-style games and toys. This is undoubtedly obvious.

Economic bankruptcy has greatly reduced China's market, and under the increasingly desolate situation, friends with full pockets are also entertaining themselves with the pleasures of sensual entertainment. Therefore, foreigners who are good at "Zigon's art" come to find their patrons in this area. The very crude national goods movement naturally cannot satisfy the desires of this group of people with high material enjoyment. Since women who pride themselves on being modern are already like this, how can they have the ability to call on these obedient and ignorant children!

Setting Up a Ring 210

— Wu Fei

The one who sets up a ring is a hero, and the one who fights in the ring is of course also a hero. Setting up a ring and fighting in a ring were common things to hear about in the past. Even several years ago, there were Ma Yongzhen and Huo Yuanjia who came to the foreign concessions of Shanghai to set up rings. But unfortunately, both of these heroes were ultimately ambushed and killed by the hands of non-heroes, which is truly a pity!

But the ring of today is indeed invisible to the eyes and inaudible to the ears. This is because there are too many "weak scholars" and "ailing beauties" in our country; and most of the martial arts enthusiasts are self-appreciatingly refined, and even if they have learned a few fancy boxing techniques, they are still not qualified to set up a ring. Moreover, in today's era of flourishing science, there is simply no ring to set up. Even if there is, it can only be said to be a game. If you really want to defeat all the invincible opponents in the world, then claiming to be a hero and a hegemon is absolutely impossible.

Anyone who sets up a ring must at least have confidence that he is extraordinary, and at the same time have considered that few people are his opponents. Even if he cannot have the expectation of having two opponents retreat at the same time, he thinks that he will not be thrown off the stage by the one who fights in the ring. Moreover, he stands firmly on the stage, and the one who goes to fight him must commit an act of insubordination. In terms of status, he always occupies some advantage; however, it is unexpected when he unfortunately encounters an opponent who throws him off the ring several feet high.

The one who sets up the ring thinks that his skills are greater than the sky, looking down on everything and despising everything; therefore, the words he speaks always carry a tone of arrogance. What "punching through the north and south two capitals," what "kicking across the two banks of the Yellow River," with imposing dignity, invincible in the world, it seems to be a bit of a menacing appearance. The one who fights in the ring also does so because: firstly, he is a little unconvinced after hearing his bragging, so he can't help but go to "try out my old man's skills," and secondly, he sees him flaunting his power and wants to strike him down, so that he can also show that he is a hero and curb his arrogance. But this also requires measuring your own strength, is it enough? If you go to do it recklessly like Kuafu chasing the sun, wouldn't that be terrible. So I say: setting up a ring is a very difficult thing, and fighting in the ring is even more difficult; this is definitely not something that everyone can set up, nor is it something that everyone can fight.

A few days ago, Zhang Xuebin of the Linji Orthodox Sect of the Shaolin Temple set up a "Plum Blossom Stake Ring" in the Great Shanghai Garden, calling for seeking teachers and visiting friends; according to him, he is not only capable of all eighteen kinds of martial arts, but also proficient in the so-called "Golden Bell Cover" and "Iron Shirt" kung fu, and is able to be invulnerable to knives and spears (?). This statement is really similar to the swordsmen described in martial arts novels. Of course, I am not an expert, and I cannot use scientific theories to prove whether he has it or not; but according to my guess, there is a bit of a lie in this.

About Raising Children for Young Couples 211

— Ying Ying

Suppose in a completely unconstrained small family. The husband is very young and the wife is beautiful enough, of course, the intensity of love between the couple need not be said; the husband's exclusive love for the wife, and the wife's tender consideration for the husband, are also directly proportional!

Page 22

However, the question is always what to do after there is a crystallization of love? Even if it does not hinder the husband, at least in the wife's responsibility, it is necessary to take care of herself and her husband, and also take care of the child.

In many cases, it often happens that after a wife has a child, she obviously shifts the weight from her husband to her child, concerning the child's clothes, food, and living. If the child is too cute, she will often unintentionally strip the husband of his entire love.

So this is extremely dangerous for couples! In the future, after the husband does not get the wife's entire exclusive love, he can easily vent on the child, from jealousy of the child to resentment! This seems like a very unnecessary thing!

However, conversely, if the couple wants to permanently maintain the solidity of their love, for the comfort of their own lives! Then, if the child lacks good care, or is completely left to others to ignore, then even more tragic events are more likely to happen!

A young mother with a child must have the dual responsibility of taking care of and loving the husband and the entire child. (Naturally, those with fixed occupations are still exceptions). She must extremely cherish everything about the child, but she must also take care of everything about the husband, so that the husband does not feel annoyed, abandoned, or even resented out of jealousy because of the child; in the same way, he can more smoothly obtain exclusive love and arouse the joy and fun of having a child!

Young mothers, what an easy but burdensome job it is!

"Its heart is also beating differently!" 212

— Yi An

Mexico's Melancholy 213

— Zhang Jun

For her melancholy, I also became melancholy::::

With two big eyes, a round black face, and always hanging the mark of melancholy on the brow is she—the other day when I asked her name, she told me the most beautiful Mexican flavor of Ramona.

(Ramona)!

Then I thought of this as a novel, which was later made into a movie, accompanied by a beautiful song of the name. So, my mouth reached her ear:

—Ramona! Do you know that you make me think of Mexico, the beaches there, the Rio Grande there, the bullfighting arena there? Your name is a song, three years ago I was hanging on the corner of my mouth all day long, singing in the coconut branches under the tropical palm trees. Now I have forgotten it; but for you, I should sing it again!

The next day, with a heart of passionate love. I was looking for "Ramona" in every sheet music sales place on North Sichuan Road: Appro Music Store, Japanese Music Store, Liangyou Company.

—"Ramona"? It's out of date!

—"Ramona"? You go to the opposite store to ask about it.

Is it really out of date? Ramona is so young, blooming like a morning sunflower. Unexpected good fortune in the last one I got this songbook; immediately looked a lot younger, walked out of the door jumping and laughing for no reason.

Quietly, without letting anyone know, I took the songbook and took advantage of the dead afternoon to hide in the flower bushes in the campus and sing; the voice was low, like a dream::::

(God, let my devout, pure, and full of loving voice be able to relieve her melancholy. It is unfortunate to paint a layer of gray powder on such a strong face: why be melancholy!)

—Why be melancholy? Because men are black-hearted; they don't let me be with people. This is such a despicable idea, I am really afraid of them:::

She told me, and suddenly leaned on my shoulder and cried.

Gently stroking her, comforting her with my most passionate words; kissing her neck, which was blackened by the water in the swimming pool and the summer sun. I remembered that beautiful song, and sang it lowly—":::Ramona, I need you my own."

Reading Q&A

News from the "Scholarly-Vocational Mutual Aid Advancement Association" 214

Mr. Editor:

Following your publication of a letter about organizing the "Scholarly-Vocational Mutual Aid Advancement Association" in your esteemed newspaper, I have received letters from a total of forty-six comrades expressing their desire to join this organization. Consequently, we convened the first preparatory meeting last Sunday evening at 8 PM. Only twenty-three people attended. (The notification letters were sent out on Saturday, so perhaps some people had not yet received them, or were unable to attend due to work commitments.) Although only half of the people attended, everyone was very excited and enthusiastic. With the exception of a few people who remained quietly silent, most people actively offered their opinions, and the principles of the charter were discussed item by item. We adjourned hurriedly around 10 PM, after hastily electing nine preparatory committee members due to time constraints.

Yesterday, the few preparatory committee members and I discussed it again. However, due to a lack of organizational experience, one problem is difficult to solve. That is, the basic fund is contributed by each member according to their ability. At the first preparatory meeting, more than fifty yuan had already been donated. The monthly membership fee has not yet been decided, but it will probably be between four and six jiao. The funds seem too small, so we urgently need to solicit more members. However, if we formally establish the association now and then solicit members, although it would be better in terms of form and organization, we would have no way to raise funds for the initial equipment, such as desks, chairs, and all necessary items. Moreover, the monthly rent would be a heavy burden. If we don't establish a headquarters and instead borrow a member's place as a mailing address, it seems too disorganized. Members would not have a good impression, and it would be difficult for members to gather for academic research. If we temporarily don't announce the establishment and first solicit members to increase the fund income, then the process will definitely be delayed. Older members who joined earlier, seeing that the progress of the association is quite slow, will inevitably become gradually indifferent (although there are a few who are still enthusiastically looking forward to it, they are, after all, a minority). Please, sir, think of a proper solution for us, and instruct us on how to proceed.

Also, is it necessary for the organization of a group to register with the municipal government? What are the registration procedures? Should we register after establishment or before establishment? If we don't have a headquarters, can we register? We also hope that you will answer in detail. Furthermore, we hope that you will publish this letter so that members who did not attend the first preparatory meeting can get a general idea, and that like-minded vocational comrades can enthusiastically join this organization. My mailing address is: Liu Feng Editorial Department, No. 14, Lane 360, Beijing Road. Wishing you peace in your writing.

Respectfully,

Huang Xu

October 4th

Page 23

Editor's Note: It is commendable that Mr. Huang and others were able to organize this group in such a short period of time, and their enthusiasm and perseverance are admirable. Now, you can formally establish it first. Regarding the headquarters, if you don't have a suitable place for the time being, you can discuss it with organizations such as the YMCA, the Municipal Higher Education Association, and the China Vocational Education Society, and temporarily borrow their places to hold meetings. In addition, you can also hold them in various parks. In the initial stage, it is not necessary to rent your own headquarters, and in fact, you do not have the ability to do so. As for regular contact, it can be handled by members with better circumstances and higher positions, using their offices or residences as temporary communication centers.

The fact that more than fifty yuan has already been donated to the fund shows everyone's enthusiasm for founding the group. However, the editor hopes that this deposit will be reserved for future regular and incidental expenses. Desks, chairs, and other items can be temporarily handled with each person's existing equipment, and there is no need to strive for comfort. Renting another house does not seem necessary at present. When starting an organization, only seek a solid foundation, and all expenses should be kept to a minimum.

All organizations should register with the authorities when they are established. You can inquire about the procedures from the Municipal Party Headquarters.

Introducing a new book: "Dead Ashes," a collection of poems by Yan Chonglou, has been published recently. The text is vivid and the illustrations are exquisite. It is now published by the Life Bookstore. If you enclose four jiao in postage stamps and send them to the Literary Society at No. 63 Pushi Road, this port, the author will send you a personally signed copy of the book.

Opening Chapter: Autumn Feelings

A gust of autumn wind blows. Light clouds and thin dew suddenly part. The clear sky reveals a round moon. A piece of pure light shines into the inner chamber. Lonely in the inner chamber, without a companion. Raising her head, she fears seeing the moon's light. The round moon shines on the shadow of separation. Sent to the long pavilion, not returning for a long time. Waiting until the end of the world, without news (In the mirror, the old form is no longer there. In dreams, they meet night after night. Not as good as expressing it once during separation. Thinking about it, tears hide in the cheeks. The man gave the woman a fragrant silk handkerchief to wipe them with. There are many affectionate women in the world. They also love the family's exquisite talent. Applying powder, beside the dressing table. Tender village, young men are easily swayed. How can there be any sour intention in my life. Endure my diligence, endure me doubly. What harm is there in calling each other sisters when we meet. Draw them together in one stroke, two people's eyebrows. Only worried about reading and occupying the good spring light. Preventing the journey, not allowing them to come. The belt is gradually widening, and the person is getting thinner. Knowing the secret feelings, the waist circumference. Intricate hairpins will buy a boat. Low discount to find the edge of the world. Thin body wants no compensation.
